## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: The task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and current population P, which is a classic population dynamics problem. The relationship likely involves density-dependent regulation, where growth rate depends on population size, possibly with time-varying environmental factors.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unrestricted growth, Malthusian)
- Logistic growth (differential form): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (density-dependent regulation via carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)) (asymmetric growth with slowing at high densities)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (P / c1)**c2) (flexible density dependence shape parameter)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P / c1 - 1) * (1 - P / c2) (depensation, negative growth at low densities)
- Time-decaying growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * P (exponential decline in reproductive rate)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t))) (periodic carrying capacity)
- Power-law density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**c2 (nonlinear per-capita growth rate)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 - c2 * P**3 (higher-order expansion of density effects)
- Logarithmic resource limitation: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) + c2 * P (alternative to logistic, Gompertz-like)
- Seasonal forcing additive: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic migration or harvesting)
- Time-varying growth with saturation: dP_dt = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) * P (gradual onset of reproductive capacity)
- Density feedback with time lag proxy: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t)) (slow environmental degradation)
- Rational density regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (saturation of resources per capita)
- Logistic with Allee (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (cubic polynomial, critical threshold)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent regulation → negative quadratic or higher-order terms in P (e.g., -c1*P**2) representing resource competition
- Allee effect → cubic polynomial in P with a negative region near P=0, producing an unstable equilibrium at low density
- Time-varying environment → parameters multiplied by explicit time functions like exp(-c*t), sin(c*t), or polynomials in t
- Asymmetric approach to carrying capacity → logarithmic function log(c/P) giving slower approach near equilibrium (Gompertz)
- Seasonal or periodic forcing → sinusoidal terms added to or multiplied by the per-capita growth rate
- Onset of reproduction or delayed growth → growth rate multiplied by an increasing bounded function like (1 - exp(-c*t))
- Scaling laws in density feedback → power-law terms P**c suggesting allometric or fractal resource use
- Ratio-dependent limitation → per-capita growth expressed as rational function P/(c+P) akin to consumer-resource saturation

- c = -0.5980
- d = -0.07683

The GT has the form: **P²*A + P*B + P*C*exp(D*P)** where A, B, C, D are specific constants.

This is exactly the form: `P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*exp(P*c3)`

Now let me check each candidate. The key question is whether each candidate can reduce to exactly this form by choosing appropriate constants.

**Candidates with form `P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*exp(P*c3) + [extra terms]`:**

For these, I need to check if the extra terms can be zeroed out.

**Candidate 1:** Extra: `c4*sin(c5*exp(c6*t) + c7)` — depends on t. Set c4=0. Then matches GT form. ✓
Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** Extra: `c4*exp(c5*sin(P*c6 + c7*t + c8))` — set c7=0, then it's `c4*exp(c5*sin(P*c6+c8))`. This can't be zeroed unless c4=0 or c5=0. If c5=0, it becomes c4*exp(0)=c4, a constant. If c4=0, it vanishes. With c4=0, we get the base form.
Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `P²c0 + Pc1 + c2*sin(P^c3*c4+c5) + c6*exp(Pc7) + c8*exp(Pc9)`. Set c2=0. Then `P²c0+Pc1+c6*exp(Pc7)+c8*exp(Pc9)`. GT has P*exp(P*d), not exp(P*d). These are different basis functions. Can't match.
Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]
